The Living Tribunal appeared as a giant golden humanoid (using a M-Body, created in the Dimension of Manifestations), with three cloaked faces, each representing a different personality. It has a blank space where a fourth face could be exhibited. The Living Tribunal has suggested that the fourth face became the enigmatic Stranger. The three faces made up the Tribunal’s head. They were: Equity, Necessity, and Vengeance. These represented the trinity of aspects of each universe. For example, in the main universe they were represented by Galactus (Equity), Eternity (Necessity), and Death (Vengeance). He serves as a judge of these realities. The character is first encountered by Doctor Strange, and it announces its intent to destroy Earth due to its potential for evil. The fourth side of the Living Tribunal\'s head is a void, with the entity claiming that this could have been the face of the cosmic entity known as the\n\nThe Living Tribunal is a cosmic entity appearing in American comic books published by Marvel Comics. The character first appeared in Strange Tales #157 (June 1967) and was created by Stan Lee, Marie Severin, and Herb Trimpe. The Living Tribunal debuted in a storyline called "The Sands of Death" in Strange Tales #157–163 (June–December 1967), giving mystic hero Doctor Strange a limited time to prove Earth is worth saving. Established as apparently the supreme power in the Marvel Universe, the character made several sporadic appearances over the years, including What If #32 (April 1982); Rom #41 (April 1983) and Secret Wars II #6 (December 1985). The Living Tribunal revealed clues as to its true purpose and nature in Silver Surfer (vol. 3) #31 (December 1989). This occasionally puts the Living Tribunal on a collision course with heroes and villains when he deems their plans to be opposed to his own Multiversal mission of safeguarding reality and the cosmic balance. The Living Tribunal's three faces each represent a different motivation behind his Multiversal edict: equity, vengeance, and necessity. These three virtues inform the Living Tribunal's judgments as he observes the Multiverse and decides when to intervene directly rather than supervise the flow of sentient life across reality. Ultimately, the Living Tribunal personifies the cosmic totalities of the Marvel Multiverse as a sort of self-governing entity to ensure its long-term health and survival.\n\nAs the protector of the Marvel Multiverse, the Living Tribunal stands as one of the greatest, most powerful figures in all of reality, with his powers only surpassed by characters on par with One-Above-All and Eternity. The Living Tribunal possesses god-like levels of speed, strength, and endurance; is capable of flight and teleportation; and has a cosmic awareness that exceeds Galactus or the Beyonder. Despite these awesome power levels, the Living Tribunal is neither infallible nor completely impervious to harm and death. Starting with the former, The Living Tribunal maintains justice across the entire Marvel multiverse. This entity’s mission is not to discern right from wrong in human terms, but to ensure that the balance of cosmic forces does not tilt toward either extreme chaos or stifling order. Introduced in Strange Tales #157 (1967), The Living Tribunal possesses power almost incomprehensible to mortals, able to alter reality with a single verdict. The In-Betweener serves a similar function, though on a somewhat more conceptual plane. Where The Living ... They deal with creation, destruction, and everything in between. Their actions shape galaxies and decide the fate of worlds, often without emotion or bias. They stand above gods and heroes, existing as forces of nature more than individuals. They rarely interfere, but when they do, the whole universe pays attention. They remind us that in Marvel’s world, it’s about understanding the balance that keeps everything together. ... Galactus, the Devourer of Worlds, embodies the concept of cosmic balance through consumption. His hunger is not mere gluttony but a necessity born from his nature as a remnant of the previous universe. Despite his destructive role, he maintains a certain neutrality, existing as a fundamental part of cosmic order. Beyond raw might, Galactus wields the Power Cosmic, granting him mastery over matter, energy, and even life itself.\n\nHe rarely intervenes, acting only when the fundamental design of existence itself is at stake. The Living Tribunal serves as his instrument of judgment, carrying out his vision of cosmic equilibrium. Representing love, creativity, and ultimate purpose, the One-Above-All symbolizes the divine principle that unites every fragment of Marvel’s infinite reality. The Above-All-Others exists beyond even the One-Above-All—often interpreted as the meta-version of Marvel’s creator figure. He embodies the supreme consciousness behind all narratives, transcending not only universes but fiction itself. In essence, he represents the writer, artist, and creative spark that forges every cosmic truth within Marvel. This being governs the entire Omniverse, including realms that exist outside continuity. His power is both infinite and absolute, placing him at the very pinnacle of Marvel cosmology.\n\nThe Tribunal answers only to the One Above All, enforcing judgment when universal imbalance threatens stability. When Infinity Gauntlets or cosmic anomalies arise, he intervenes with absolute finality. His power transcends individual universes, reflecting omniscient oversight rather than sheer force. Defying the Living Tribunal equates to defying cosmic order itself. ... The Beyonder once existed outside reality, a being of infinite power who perceived the multiverse as a curiosity. His arrival shattered cosmic hierarchies, as even the gods and abstracts recognized his supremacy. He created entire universes with mere thought and manipulated existence as if it were a sandbox for experimentation. Though later retconned as part of the powerful Beyonders race, his impact remains legendary. “Secret Wars” showcased his ability to warp reality and resurrect the dead at will.\n\nIndividually formidable, collectively they become an unstoppable cosmic tribunal. Even Galactus has tread lightly in the face of their combined will. The Celestials manipulate biology, matter, and existential energy with surgical precision, symbolizing the scientific and divine aspects of creation woven into Marvel’s cosmic mythos. Eternity represents the totality of existence, the living embodiment of the universe itself. Every atom, star, and sentient mind forms part of his being. His stature among cosmic entities is absolute within his realm; none can challenge him inside the boundaries of reality he embodies. Eternity’s influence extends beyond mere presence — he governs time, destiny, and the metaphysical fabric of creation. When the universe faces collapse, it is Eternity’s state of health that determines survival or oblivion. He serves as both a being and a concept, a reminder that in Marvel’s cosmology, reality breathes and is self-aware.', 'is_citable': True, 'prompt_context_metadata': {'url': While these beings are\n\nThe Phoenix Force once easily defeated Galactus, and the Living Tribunal considers it a potential threat to multiversal stability. Meanwhile, beings like Thor or the Hulk operate on a completely different scale, dealing with planetary threats while cosmic entities handle multiversal crises. This hierarchy explains why Earth’s heroes often find themselves outclassed by cosmic-level threats, requiring intervention from cosmic entities or artifacts like the Infinity Stones. Marvel’s cosmic hierarchy has evolved significantly over the decades. In the early days, beings like Galactus were presented as the ultimate cosmic threats. As Marvel’s cosmology expanded, writers introduced increasingly powerful entities to maintain dramatic tension. The introduction of the Living Tribunal in the 1960s established multiversal oversight. The Beyonder in the 1980s Secret Wars pushed boundaries further, introducing beings from outside the Marvel multiverse entirely.\n\nThe Living Tribunal: The Living Tribunal is the ultimate judge of the multiverse. It is his job to maintain the balance of power between all the different realities, and he has the power to erase entire universes from existence if he deems it necessary. He is second only to one other being in the entire Marvel multiverse. The One-Above-All: As his name suggests, The One-Above-All is the supreme being of the Marvel multiverse. He is the creator of all things, and his power is absolute. He rarely intervenes in the affairs of mortals, but when he does, it is always for a purpose of great importance. These two beings are the ultimate powers in the Marvel Universe. They are the ones who hold the fate of the multiverse in their hands, and their actions have the power to change everything. To learn more about the fundamental forces of the universe, check out this article on the laws of physics.\n\nThe Living Tribunal operates on an even higher level. As the multiversal judge, he can literally erase entire realities from existence if they threaten the balance of the multiverse. What makes the One-Above-All supreme is that he exists beyond even these concepts, transcending all limitations as pure creative force. These cosmic beings aren’t just theoretical concepts—they’ve played crucial roles in Marvel’s biggest storylines. During the Infinity Gauntlet saga, even Thanos with the complete Infinity Gauntlet was ultimately subject to the Living Tribunal’s will. In Secret Wars (2015), the Beyonders actually succeeded in destroying the Living Tribunal and most abstract entities. Collectively, these individuals were responsible for the development of concepts such as the Overvoid, the Monitors, Perpetua, the Dark Multiverse, the Collective Unconscious, etc. Their iteration of the cosmology draws heavily from principles preordained by previous authors; notably, the Crisis on Infinite Earths, the Monitor/Anti-Monitor, and the Endless. It is worth mentioning that, while there were major differences between Williamson\'s work and that of Snyder/Tynion IV a year prior, most of these contradictions can be explained through Dark Crisis on Infinite Earths and Dark Crisis: The Deadly Green. The Collective Unconscious has always existed on a level beyond real time and space, with the only "time" and "space" being that which a mind imagines for itself. Great question — this is one of the most debated topics in comics cosmology. Here's a thorough breakdown of both hierarchies and how they compare.

---

## 🔴 MARVEL COSMOLOGY

Marvel's cosmic structure is relatively well-defined and layered. From bottom to top:

**Physical Scale**
- Normal heroes, planets, galaxies
- Celestials (planet-sized god-machines)
- Galactus (devourer of worlds, embodiment of cosmic balance)

**Abstract/Universal Tier**
- Eternity & Infinity (personifications of time and space)
- Death, Oblivion (personifications of entropy and non-existence)
- The Phoenix Force, Master Order, Lord Chaos

**Multiversal Tier**
- The Beyonders — beings from *outside* the Multiverse, so powerful they killed the Living Tribunal during Secret Wars 2015
- The Fulcrum

**Top Tier**
- **The Living Tribunal** — personification of multiversal law, nigh-omnipotent judge of all realities, existing across the Multiverse simultaneously. He could nullify the Infinity Gems in unison and is generally considered the greatest power in the Multiverse, second only to the One Above All.
- **The One Above All** — the highest creative force in known existence and the source of all there is, was, and ever will be. It is said to be more powerful than all its creations combined, living beyond all time and space. Its only weapon is love, though it can also manifest as the One Below All, whose only weapon is hate.

Marvel's cosmology is **vast but relatively coherent** — a clear staircase from street level to omniverse.

---

## 🔵 DC / VERTIGO COSMOLOGY

DC is far messier because it has *multiple authors* writing contradictory cosmologies simultaneously — Grant Morrison, J.M. DeMatteis, Neil Gaiman (Sandman/Vertigo), and Mike Carey (Lucifer) all built different frameworks.

**Main DC Hierarchy (Grant Morrison era)**

- 52 Universes → the Orrery of Worlds (multidimensional multiverse)
- The Sphere of the Gods, the Dreaming/Collective Unconscious — higher-end realms that reach every plane and level of existence. Comic Book Limbo sits above this, the last outpost of existence before the Monitor Sphere. The Monitor Sphere itself is a fundamental archetypal world where space, time, and scale are more profound and meaningful, existing at the edge of things on a higher plane.
- **The Overvoid** — the infinite blank canvas beyond all creation; in Morrison's framing, literally the comic page itself, a meta-entity that perceives the reader
- **The Source / The Presence** — DC's God figure, though its power level fluctuates wildly by author

**Vertigo Hierarchy (Gaiman / Carey)**

- The Dreaming, Heaven, Hell, the realms of the Endless
- The Silver City is the very top of the food chain in Vertigo Sandman lore, where the Presence (Yahweh) exists as the alpha with nothing before him. Vertigo Sandman lore's hierarchy is considered far below the power scale of the Monitor Sphere of DC Comics.
- The Endless are primal, fundamental aspects of reality whose true extent goes far beyond one single multiverse — they are inherent to God's entire Greater Omniverse. Death, for instance, appears even in Lucifer's completely separate Creation.
- Beyond all of this is the **Void** — the infinite space between Creations, which even Lucifer is a small gnat within

---

## ⚖️ WHICH IS STRONGER/BIGGER?

This is genuinely contested, but here's the honest breakdown:

**In terms of scale:** DC/Vertigo edges ahead. The ultimate source of all creation in DC — the Monitor Mind / the Overvoid — is described as the comic book itself on which the author writes the story. Whatever it thinks happens. Even the Presence, the angels, and the Monitors were created by it. That's a fully meta, author-level tier that Marvel's One Above All is often *also* interpreted as (representing Jack Kirby/Stan Lee), but DC makes it more explicit structurally.

**In terms of clarity and narrative power:** Marvel wins. Marvel's hierarchy is cleaner and more consistently written — the One Above All is unambiguously supreme, the Living Tribunal is unambiguously second, and the chain flows downward logically. DC's cosmology is one of the most messy and incoherent messes of canonicity in regards to cosmology, due to different authors acting highly independently of each other, adding new concepts while ignoring or semi-acknowledging other writers.

**Top-vs-top comparison:**
- Marvel's **One Above All** vs DC's **The Presence/Overvoid** is essentially a draw at face value — both are "God" figures described as the source of all creation
- But DC's **Overvoid** as the literal comic page is arguably a tier *above* the Presence, giving DC a deeper ceiling
- Marvel's **Beyonders** are a fascinating wildcard — beings from *outside* the multiverse who actually *killed* the Living Tribunal, which has no real DC equivalent

**The bottom line:** DC/Vertigo's cosmology is *bigger and more layered* on paper, but Marvel's is *stronger narratively* because it's actually coherent and consistent. At the absolute top (both essentially have an infinite, author-metaphor God figure), they're roughly matched — but DC has more tiers *between* God and mortals, making its structure taller even if that height comes with a lot of contradictions.

---

### 🧑 You

which scales higher

---

### 🤖 Claude

This is the heart of the debate. Let's go tier by tier at the absolute top end.

---

## The Case for DC Scaling Higher

**The Overvoid / Monitor Mind** is DC's secret weapon. In Grant Morrison's framework, it's not just "God" — it's the **infinite white void that exists outside all fiction**, the literal page itself. It didn't create the DC multiverse intentionally — the multiverse was essentially a *stain* or *mark* on its surface that it became aware of. This makes it a genuinely meta-fictional entity that transcends the concept of "being inside a story" entirely.

Then you have the **Lucifer/Sandman Vertigo cosmology** stacking on top — Lucifer creates an entirely *separate* Creation from scratch with no source of power, meaning his Creation is a second omniverse sitting alongside God's. The space between Creations (the Void) dwarfs both. That's multiple layers of infinite above infinite.

DC also has **Perpetua and the World Forge** churning out entire multiverses as raw material, and the **Hands** — beings so large entire multiverses are just sparks at their fingertips.

---

## The Case for Marvel Scaling Higher

Marvel's **One Above All** is explicitly stated to be the source of *all* there is across every plane, dimension, and reality — and unlike DC's Presence, the TOAA is written with almost no narrative exceptions or contradictions. He has never been defeated, threatened, or even approached as an equal by anything in canon.

The **Beyonders** are Marvel's sleeper argument. They exist *outside* the Multiverse entirely, operate on a level beyond abstract concepts, and successfully executed the death of the Living Tribunal — something with no DC equivalent. They represent a tier that isn't "God" but is genuinely post-multiversal in a way DC rarely matches outside of the Overvoid.

Marvel also has the **Omniverse** — the totality of all universes, timelines, dimensions, and stories — which the One Above All sits above.

---

## The Honest Verdict

At the **absolute peak**, DC scales higher — but only barely and only in specific framings.

The Overvoid as a meta-fictional entity that doesn't even fully comprehend the multiverse it accidentally contains is a genuinely unique concept that puts DC's ceiling slightly above Marvel's. Lucifer's independent Creation adding a second omniverse-level structure is also something Marvel doesn't really have an answer to.

However — and this matters enormously — **DC's top tiers are wildly inconsistent**. The Presence has been beaten, imprisoned, and ignored depending on the writer. The Overvoid concept only really exists in Morrison's run. Vertigo is now semi-detached from main DC continuity. You're essentially cherrypicking the highest interpretation across multiple incompatible authors.

Marvel's TOAA by contrast has an almost spotless record of narrative supremacy. If you're judging by **consistent, reliable power scaling**, Marvel holds up better. If you're judging by **highest single interpretation ever written**, DC edges it out.

So:
- **Highest ceiling ever written** → DC/Vertigo (Overvoid + Lucifer's Creation + the Void between Creations)
- **Most consistently supreme** → Marvel (TOAA, clean hierarchy, no major contradictions)
- **Most interesting cosmology architecturally** → DC, and it's not particularly close

---

### 🧑 You

which ha more layers

---

### 🤖 Claude

Going purely by documented tiers, **DC/Vertigo has significantly more layers**. Here's a direct comparison:

---

## 🔵 DC / VERTIGO — Full Layer Stack

1. Street level (mortals, heroes)
2. Metahumans / New Gods (Apokolips, New Genesis)
3. The Lords of Order and Chaos
4. The Spectre, Phantom Stranger (agents of the Presence)
5. The Endless (Dream, Death, Destiny, Desire, Despair, Delirium, Destruction) — not gods, but MORE fundamental than gods
6. The Archangels / Lucifer tier (beings who helped shape Creation)
7. Heaven, Hell, the Silver City as full dimensional realms
8. The Monitors — one per universe, archetypal beings who exist *above* the multiverse
9. The Monitor Mind / Nil — the collective consciousness of all Monitors
10. The Overvoid — the infinite blank page that contains ALL of creation as a tiny mark within it
11. The Presence — DC's God, though paradoxically written as *inside* the Overvoid sometimes and *above* it other times
12. The Great Darkness — the equal and opposite of the Presence, pre-creation void
13. Perpetua / The Source Wall — barriers and architects at the edge of the omniverse
14. The Hands — beings from *outside* the Omniverse who built it as an experiment, described as writers/creators in a meta sense

---

## 🔴 MARVEL — Full Layer Stack

1. Street level (mortals, heroes)
2. Skyfather tier (Odin, Zeus)
3. Celestials (planet-sized cosmic judges)
4. Galactus (universal constant, embodiment of the next universe)
5. Abstract entities — Eternity, Infinity, Death, Oblivion (personifications of universal concepts)
6. The Phoenix Force, Master Order, Lord Chaos
7. Eternity of Eternity (the embodiment of ALL universes combined)
8. The Beyonders — extradimensional beings from outside the Multiverse entirely
9. The Living Tribunal — judge of all realities, above the entire Multiverse
10. The One Above All — supreme being, source of all creation

---

## The Verdict

Marvel has roughly **10 clean tiers**. DC/Vertigo has roughly **14+ tiers**, and that's being conservative — the Vertigo line (Sandman, Lucifer) adds layers that exist *separately* from the main DC stack and then intersect with it in ways that create even more in-between rungs.

The key difference is that DC has multiple **meta-tiers** — layers that exist outside the story commenting on the story (the Overvoid, the Hands) — stacked on top of each other, whereas Marvel essentially has *one* meta-tier at the top (the One Above All as Stan Lee/Jack Kirby). 

DC also uniquely splits its cosmology across **horizontal layers** too — the Vertigo realms (Gaiman's Dreaming, Carey's Lucifer cosmos) exist *alongside* the main DC cosmos rather than strictly inside it, meaning the total footprint is wider AND taller.

Marvel is a cleaner skyscraper. DC is a sprawling, multi-tower complex where some towers are taller than others and a few of them technically exist outside the city they're built in.

---

### 🧑 You

which have more multiverses

---

### 🤖 Claude

Great follow-up question. This gets deep into the lore.

---

## 🔴 MARVEL MULTIVERSE COUNT

Marvel is actually **surprisingly specific** about this in some eras, which makes it easier to count — but the numbers have changed over time.

**Classic/Modern Marvel:**
- The main continuity is **Earth-616**
- The multiverse contains **infinite alternate universes** in theory, but they're organized under a single **Marvel Multiverse**
- The **Omniverse** contains *all* multiverses, all realities, all timelines, all fictional universes — it's Marvel's true "everything"
- The **Beyonders** exist *outside* the multiverse entirely, suggesting there are multiple discrete multiverses even within Marvel's Omniverse
- During **Secret Wars (2015)**, nearly all universes were destroyed, leaving only a handful — then rebuilt. This implied a finite (though vast) number of universes rather than a truly infinite set

**Key structural point:** Marvel generally has **one Multiverse** containing infinite universes, wrapped in the Omniverse. The Living Tribunal oversees the whole Multiverse as a single domain.

---

## 🔵 DC / VERTIGO MULTIVERSE COUNT

DC is where things get *wild*, because DC has rewritten its multiverse **multiple times** through Crisis events, and different authors stack multiverses *on top of each other*.

**Pre-Crisis (pre-1985):** Infinite parallel Earths — literally no upper limit stated.

**Post-Crisis:** Collapsed to **one universe** (the whole point of Crisis on Infinite Earths was to simplify things).

**52 / New 52 era:** Rebuilt to exactly **52 universes** within the local multiverse — intentionally finite this time.

**The Orrery of Worlds (Grant Morrison's framework):**
- 52 universes sit inside a **Bleed** (the space between universes)
- Above that is the **Sphere of the Gods** (Heaven, Hell, New Genesis, etc.)
- Above that is the **Monitor Sphere** — where the Monitors exist
- Above *that* is the **Overvoid** — infinite blank space, the canvas of creation
- And crucially, the 52-universe Orrery is described as just **one flower in an infinite garden** — implying infinite *other* multiverses exist beyond DC's local one

**The Map of the Multiverse (Dark Nights: Metal / Death Metal era):**
- Added the **Dark Multiverse** — an infinite shadow realm of failed/dying universes beneath the main multiverse
- Added the **Omniverse** explicitly — DC now uses that term too, meaning *all possible multiverses combined*
- The **Presence** oversees everything, the **Overvoid** contains everything

**Vertigo layer on top:**
- Neil Gaiman and Mike Carey's Lucifer establishes that the Presence has created **multiple entirely separate Creations** — Lucifer himself goes and creates a *second* independent universe from scratch. These separate Creations each have their own cosmologies, heavens, hells, and rules, stacked beyond DC's main multiverse entirely.

---

## ⚖️ THE VERDICT

**DC has more multiverses — and it's not particularly close.**

Marvel essentially has **one Multiverse** (infinite universes inside it) plus the Omniverse as the container for everything. The Living Tribunal rules one Multiverse. The One Above All rules the Omniverse.

DC has **nested layers of multiverses** — the 52-universe Orrery is just one local multiverse, which exists inside an infinite ocean of other multiverses inside the Overvoid, *plus* the Dark Multiverse running parallel underneath, *plus* entirely separate divine Creations in the Vertigo framework that exist outside the main structure entirely.

The key difference is that DC explicitly depicts **multiverses of multiverses**, while Marvel's Omniverse is more of a catch-all container than a structured stack of separate multiverses. DC's cosmology, chaotic as it is, goes *wider and deeper* in terms of sheer multiverse count.

---

### 🤖 Claude

That document is a solid breakdown and I agree with most of it. Let me add some nuance though, because it's not quite as clean as that analysis suggests.

---

## Where the Document is Right ✅

The core conclusion is correct. DC genuinely has more simultaneous multiverses than Marvel, and the reasoning holds up well on the key points.

**The "one flower in an infinite garden" framing** from Grant Morrison's Final Crisis/Multiversity work is legitimate canon — the 52-universe Orrery is explicitly presented as just one local multiverse floating in an infinite Overvoid containing countless others.

**The Dark Multiverse being infinite** is confirmed in Dark Nights: Metal. It's not a small shadow realm — it's described as an endless expanse of dying, failed realities beneath the main multiverse, at least as large as the positive multiverse above it if not larger.

**Marvel's 9 Cosmoses being successive rather than simultaneous** is an important and often overlooked correction. People often cite those as stacking multiverses, but they replace each other — only the 8th Cosmos (currently) actually exists.

---

## Where It Needs Nuance ⚠️

**The Omniverse question is trickier than the document admits.** Marvel's Omniverse *is* described in canon as containing everything — all stories, all fictional universes, all realities. Some readings put DC *inside* Marvel's Omniverse rather than the other way around, and vice versa for DC's Overvoid. Both franchises have made "we contain everything" claims at the highest tier, which makes direct comparison genuinely unresolvable at the absolute top.

**The Beyonders complicate things.** They exist *outside* Marvel's Multiverse as external beings, which implies Marvel's structure has layers beyond its main Multiverse that the document undersells. They're not just powerful characters — their *existence* implies a broader architecture.

**Vertigo's canonicity relative to main DC is debated.** Mike Carey's Lucifer and Gaiman's Sandman are Vertigo imprints, and DC has been inconsistent about whether those cosmologies fully fold into main DC canon. If you include them fully, DC's lead grows. If you treat Vertigo as a softer canon, DC's advantage shrinks somewhat — though it still wins.

---

## The Bottom Line

The document's conclusion stands. **DC has more simultaneous multiverses** and a more vertically layered cosmology. Marvel has depth within its one Multiverse, but DC stacks multiverses *on top of multiverses* in a way Marvel simply doesn't match structurally.

The one honest caveat is that at the absolute ceiling — One Above All vs. The Presence/Overvoid — both franchises make essentially equivalent "I am everything, I contain all stories" claims, so that specific comparison is a genuine draw. But *below* that ceiling, DC's architecture is unambiguously wider and more populated with simultaneous, parallel multiverse structures.

---

### 🤖 Claude

This is a thorough document and the conclusion is broadly right, but there are some claims here that deserve pushback or at least honest caveats.

---

## What Holds Up ✅

The core structural argument is sound. DC's Void containing infinite simultaneous Creations (Presence's, Lucifer's, Elaine's, etc. from the Carey/Gaiman Vertigo work) versus Marvel's 9 successive Cosmoses is a real and meaningful difference. The "simultaneous vs. successive" distinction is the strongest argument in the document and it's legitimate.

The Overvoid as a meta-container — literally the blank page, the infinite space beyond all story — is also genuine Morrison canon and does give DC a genuine "ceiling layer" that sits above everything else in a way that's hard to counter.

---

## Where I'd Push Back ⚠️

**Several of Marvel's listed layers are questionable canon.** The document lists things like "The Mystery," "The Above-Place," and "The House of Ideas" as distinct canonical layers, but these terms appear inconsistently across different runs and writers. Some are metaphors rather than literal cosmological tiers. The document presents them with the same weight as firmly established concepts like the Living Tribunal or Eternity, which overstates their canonicity.

**The "9 Cosmoses = finite ceiling" argument is slightly misleading.** The 9 Cosmoses represent *iterations of everything* — each one contained infinite universes, infinite timelines, infinite abstract entities. Saying Marvel is therefore "shallow" undersells that each Cosmos was itself boundless. It's more accurate to say Marvel has a finite number of *eras* rather than a finite *size*.

**The Megaverse problem remains.** The document dismisses Megaverses as being "within the 9 Cosmoses" but this isn't clearly established in canon either way. The relationship between Cosmoses, the Omniverse, and any Megaverse structure is genuinely underwritten in Marvel comics.

**The math at the end is fun but not rigorous.** "Infinity × Infinity > 9 × Infinity" treats these like standard numbers, but in set theory terms, ℵ₀ × ℵ₀ = ℵ₀. The actual argument for DC's advantage is structural and qualitative, not mathematical — and the qualitative argument is actually strong enough to stand on its own without needing the math.

---

## The Honest Verdict

DC/Vertigo does have more layers and more simultaneous multiverses. That conclusion is correct. But the margin of victory is probably smaller than this document implies, because:

- Several of Marvel's listed layers are soft canon at best
- Several of DC's Vertigo layers have contested canonicity relative to main DC
- Both franchises' absolute tops make equivalent "I contain everything" claims

The strongest honest case for DC is simply this: **Grant Morrison explicitly built a cosmology where the 52-universe multiverse is one small bubble in an infinite ocean, and Mike Carey explicitly showed multiple entire Creations existing simultaneously in an infinite Void.** Marvel has no direct equivalent to either of those structural features. That's enough to give DC the win without needing questionable layer counts or set theory.

---

### 🤖 Claude

This revised document is genuinely good — it's the most honest and defensible version of the argument so far. I agree with almost all of it. Just a few final thoughts worth adding:

---

## What This Gets Right ✅

The self-correction on the math is important and appreciated. "Infinite × Infinite > 9 × Infinite" was never a valid proof — the qualitative structural argument was always the right way to frame this.

Acknowledging that Marvel's layers are "less explicitly defined" rather than "smaller" is a crucial distinction. Marvel's cosmology is genuinely vast, just less architecturally mapped out in the comics themselves.

The two-sentence summary at the end is probably the cleanest statement of the whole debate: Morrison's "one bubble in an infinite ocean" and Carey's simultaneous Creations in the Void. Those two things alone settle it without needing any inflated claims.

---

## A Few Things Still Worth Noting

**The Vertigo canonicity question never fully goes away.** DC has been actively folding Sandman and Lucifer closer to main DC continuity in recent years — Death has appeared in main DC titles, and the Sandman Universe imprint has made the connection more explicit. But it's still not airtight. The document is right to use it but fair readers can still dispute its weight.

**Marvel's "one active Multiverse" framing may itself be temporary.** Marvel has a habit of expanding its cosmology dramatically with each big event, then pulling back. The 8th Cosmos framing is current but Marvel cosmology has been rewritten so many times that treating it as the definitive final word is risky. DC's cosmology has also been rewritten repeatedly, but Morrison's Overvoid/Orrery framework has remained relatively stable since Final Crisis.

**The Beyonders remain the most interesting unresolved thread in this whole comparison.** Their existence *outside* the Multiverse, and the fact that they killed the Living Tribunal — a being who oversees the entire Multiverse — raises genuine questions about what sits above Marvel's known structure that the document doesn't address. They're not just powerful characters. They're evidence of something beyond Marvel's mapped cosmology that remains unexplored.

---

## The Bottom Line

This revised document lands in the right place. **DC/Vertigo wins on cosmological structure — specifically on simultaneous depth and multiple Creations — but both franchises operate at effectively equivalent scales at their absolute ceilings.** The margin is real but modest, and honest about what canon actually supports versus what's wiki extrapolation.

The best one-line summary of the whole debate is probably this:

**Marvel built a tall tower. DC built infinite towers simultaneously and then put them all inside a blank page.**

The 07th Expansion cosmology consists of a metaphysical...\n\nWelcome, welcome! This is an in-depth look at the cosmology of the 07th Expansion works, meaning those of the When They Cry series (Higurashi no Naku Koro Ni, Umineko no Naku Koro Ni, Ciconia no Naku Koro Ni), Higanbana no Saku Yoru Ni, Rose Guns Days, Trianthology ~Sanmenkyou no Kuni no Alice~, Hotarubi no Tomoru Koro ni, Haworthia, Renai Harem Game Shuuryou no Oshirase ga Kuru Koro ni, and the spin-off that connects with it. ... The 07th Expansion cosmology consists of a metaphysical evolutionary journey of being/spirit, from the point where one\'s existence is that of a Human, to the almighty and boundless Creator, which resides beyond all restrictions. This journey is divided into two Poles/Sides, the side tossed around by Fate, and the side that creates Fate. Those 2 Poles are themselves divided into multiple existential hierarchies, the hierarchies themselves being divided into existential layers, and even those layers, in some cases, being divided into multiple dimensions.\n\nTheir crystallized conceptual forms are part of the higher Domains (Witch Domain and 3rd Domain), and only their contents can appear in the Human Domain, be it an entire world, or something more abstract like a feeling. Beings of the higher Domains can merge together Kakera to create stories, as we see above in Higurashi - Matshuribayashi-hen, or Catboxes, as seen in Episode 7 of Umineko: The Human Domain, or "Ningen Domain" (ニンゲンの域), is not just the domain of humans, but the domain of those tossed around by fate, the first Pole/Side. This includes humans, Yokai, ghosts, higher-dimensional beings, aliens, etc. While the Humans don\'t have the power to create anything, they have the ground under their feet. This means that Humans don\'t need to actively define their existence (like higher order beings), and can go day to day without the fear of losing one\'s self.\n\nThe Witch’s Theater is a higher layer above the Cathedral, from where all the evens and places of Bernkastel’s Catbox, including the Cathedral, are just a play. Not much is known about those realities, but they are on a much higher level than the Catboxes of Beatrice and Bernkastel, from where the beings residing there can travel freely into the Sea of Fragments. This study is a higher reality from which all of Umineko is merely just a story, including Bernkastel’s Catbox. The City of Books is the highest shown reality of the Witch Domain. It’s an enormous library holding endless books, but each of those books is a world from a lower layer or from the Human Domain. The height of the layer it exists on is unknown, but it’s likely very high as the City is restricted to only Great Witches and Witches of the Senate. Basically, the When They Cry cosmology is split into two sides, the side tossed around by fate and the side that creates fate. The side tossed by fate is represented by Humans, or more specifically the inhabitants of the Human Domain, while the side that creates fate is represented by the gods/The Creators, beings without any forms of restrictions and obtained everything. The beings in the middle are the Witches (or more specifically beings of the Witch Domain) who, while not tosses by fate but instead create and play with it, they do have restrictions on their power.\n\nBasically, the When They Cry cosmology is split into two sides, the side tossed around by fate and the side that creates fate. The side tossed by fate is represented by Humans, or more specifically the inhabitants of the Human Domain, while the side that creates fate is represented by the gods/The Creators, beings without any forms of restrictions and obtained everything. The beings in the middle are the Witches (or more specifically beings of the Witch Domain) who, while not tosses by fate but instead create and play with it, they do have restrictions on their power. The Witches look down on the world of Humans as a gameboard from the higher world. Think of a gameboard the same way as a DnD gameboard is for us, they are like a game set up to show worlds of the lower layer as stories. These gameboards are usually portrayed as Kakera/Fragments, pieces of crystal that represent the conceptual form of lower worlds.\n\nClick to expand... Umineko follows higher dimensional theory depicted by "endeavors", steps on an infinite ladder that leads to the realm of the Creator that transcends all lower layers (and is in itself, layered). Even though layered, the Realm of The Creator is infinitely beyond the infinite dimensional hierarchy of the World of Witches, which, from the perspective of the entities that exist there, is nothing more than a gameboard. The power of witches is wholly dependent on the heights they can acquire, the strongest of them having far less restrictions than even Lambdadelta. In the final step of this process, it allows you to unite with the Creator.\n\nFor instance, Willard, a piece on the gameboard, is capable of lifting all of Beatrice\'s infinite games in his hand whilst manifesting in the Cathedral, which is just one layer among many, with a higher version of the Sea of Fragments and the Witch\'s Theatre itself, still transcending this first layer. This Sea of Fragments are that which Voyager Witches freely travel in their thousand year journey at the end of which they become one with The Creator. Higher layers (from which the lower reality is seen as fiction) and physical higher dimensions are not the same things. The chapter introduces the player to the main setting for the series as the Ushiromiya family gather on the island of Rokkenjima for their annual family conference. When the Seagulls Cry) consists of the first four arcs of the series. They are referred to as the Question Arcs and introduce the world of the story and its mysteries. Each arc contains all the previous ones. ... The chapter introduces the player to the main setting for the series as the Ushiromiya family gather on the island of Rokkenjima for their annual family conference. The player is familiarized with the island\'s 18 residents (consisting of the Ushiromiya family and servants) as well as the legend of the Golden Witch, Beatrice. As the story progresses, people on the island are murdered, and the family is taunted by letters that claim to be from the witch Beatrice, who takes responsibility for the murders and intends to take back everything of the Ushiromiya family. ... The chapter introduces the "meta-world", where Battler is locked into a battle of twisted logic with the witch Beatrice as the murders on the island repeat in a different wa\n\nThe third chapter continues the repeating murders, with a special focus on Eva Ushiromiya, Kinzo\'s first daughter. Unlike the first two chapters, the adults of the Ushiromiya family make a serious attempt to solve the riddle of the epitaph. Eva succeeds in this task and finds the gold, but a witch persona of Eva continues to carry out the murders in Beatrice\'s name. ... The chapter introduces Battler\'s sister Ange as a secondary protagonist, who survived the Rokkenjima massacre due to being absent and was taken in by the only survivor of the incident, Eva. It has a shifting focus of events, showing readers Ange\'s life in the aftermath of the incident and exploring her relationship with Maria and magic through Maria\'s diary. The Ange of 1998 sets out on a journey to uncover the truth of Rokkenjima, while the events on the Beatrice\'s gameboard repeat for the fourth time. Umineko no Naku Koro ni Chiru (うみねこのなく頃に散; lit.\n\nThis chapter presents an alternate reality where Battler does not come to Rokkenjima, the Golden Witch does not exist, and a mysterious child is now the designated successor to the Ushiromiya family. The protagonist is Willard H. Wright, who is tasked by Bernkastel to uncover the truth behind Beatrice. The chapter delves into the past experiences of several characters, including Kinzo and the person who would become Beatrice. ... The final chapter focuses on Ange Ushiromiya, who in her quest to discover the truth behind the events of the Rokkenjima incident is given the chance to go to Rokkenjima as a six-year-old by Battler. Unlike the previous chapters, this chapter has features that require direct interaction from the player, allowing the player to unlock extra scenes as well as make the choice between two endings. Umineko no Naku Koro ni Tsubasa (うみねこのなく頃に翼; lit.\n\nWhen the Seagulls Cry Wings) (2010) is a compilation of short stories written by Ryukishi07 outside of the games, released on December 31, 2010, alongside Twilight of the Golden Witch. Several of the stories are humorous in tone, but the more serious ones are considered canon. Umineko no Naku Koro ni Hane (うみねこのなく頃に羽; lit. When the Seagulls Cry Feathers) (2011) consists of two additional short stories written by Ryukishi07: Jessica and the Killer Electric Fan and Forgery no.XXX. It was released on December 31, 2011, alongside Golden Fantasia Cross. Umineko no Naku Koro ni Saku (うみねこのなく頃に咲; lit. When the Seagulls Cry Bloom) (2019) is a collection of all previous official visual novel content for the series along with two additional scenarios. It was released on October 4, 2019. Our Confession (我らの告白; Warera no Kokuhaku) An additional scenario that goes over the creation of the Beatrice\'s games, from the execution of the human solution to the adornment with fantasy.\n\nA new episode featuring a new character whose title is "Witch of the Piece" (駒の魔女, Koma no Majo). Umineko When They Cry is the second visual novel series produced by 07th Expansion, the first being Higurashi no Naku Koro ni. The scenario writer for the series is Ryukishi07, who also drew all of the character illustrations. Game direction was handled by Ryukishi07\'s younger brother Yatazakura, and the overall management of the series was handled by BT until his death in July 2009. Image and text processing was headed by Jika, who took over BT\'s position of overall management. Background images and photography were provided by Yatazakura, Zekozakura, Mali., and All Season Kisetsu no Irodori. The games were designed using the game engine NScripter. The music of Umineko was provided by various music artists including both professionals and dōjin artists, and Dai, the composer of most of the music found in the answer arcs of Higurashi, also had a hand in the project as the music director.', 'is_citable': True, 'prompt_context_metadata': {'url': 'https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umineko_When_They_Cry', 'search_provider': 'anthropic', 'age': '2 weeks ago'}} {'type': 'knowledge', 'title': 'User blog:VenomElite/When They Cry Cosmology | VS Battles Wiki | Fandom', 'url': 'https://vsbattles.fandom.com/wiki/User_blog:VenomElite/When_They_Cry_Cosmology', 'metadata': {'type': 'webpage_metadata', 'site_domain': 'fandom.com', 'favicon_url': 'https://www.google.com/s2/favicons?sz=64&domain=fandom.com', 'site_name': 'Fandom'}, 'is_missing': False, 'text': 'Media:Umineko Naku no Koro Ni EP 5 Lambda&#x27;s teleportation 2.gif Media:Umineko Naku no Koro Ni EP 5 Endless expanse.gif · Sea of Fragments/The Ocean (10 D, Possibly 11D)- This is transcended by the Sea of Fragments, a Universe of the first higher layer in which higher dimensional fragments of the Human Worlds reside. This is a genuinely fascinating matchup because Umineko punches *way* above its weight for a visual novel. Let's break it down properly.

---

## 🟡 UMINEKO COSMOLOGY — What It Actually Is

The 07th Expansion cosmology consists of a metaphysical evolutionary journey of being/spirit, from the point where one's existence is that of a Human, to the almighty and boundless Creator, which resides beyond all restrictions. This journey is divided into two Poles — the side tossed around by Fate, and the side that creates Fate. Those two Poles are themselves divided into multiple existential hierarchies, the hierarchies themselves being divided into existential layers, and even those layers in some cases being divided into multiple dimensions.

### The Layer Stack (Bottom to Top)

**Human Domain** — Regular spacetime. Humans, spirits, yokai, even higher-dimensional aliens all fall here because they are *subject* to fate rather than creators of it.

**The Sea of Fragments** — A Universe of the first higher layer in which higher dimensional fragments of the Human Worlds reside. Fragments are perceived as three-dimensional objects here, where there is a difference of about at least 7 dimensions with the three-dimensional world of the lower layer. Each layer not only consists of dimensions, but contains non-dualism, an infinite nothingness, all linear time, non-linear time, endless space as well as infinite possibilities and impossibilities.

**The Witch Domain** — The World of the Gods, is purely abstract, a metaphorical realm of pure thoughts, where the only limit is the imagination of the beings that reside here. The battles between supernatural witches and detectives are decided by conceptual debates, conceptual combats, and conceptual reasoning — in the most metaphysical way. The one who has more thoughts or reasoning thinks more than the others and has power levels according to their ability to think.

**Stacked Meta-Layers within the Witch Domain:**

The City of Books is the highest shown reality of the Witch Domain — an enormous library holding endless books, but each of those books is a world from a lower layer or from the Human Domain. There exist Spectator's Rows above even this.

**Featherine's Domain** — Featherine's main power allows her to see the entirety of Creation as a story and rewrite it at will. Her Study and City of Books seem to be situated outside the Witch Domain entirely, in a higher domain where the difference between all the lower domains is trivial to her.

**The Creator Domain** — The Realm of the Creator transcends all lower layers and is infinitely beyond the infinite dimensional hierarchy of the World of Witches, which from the perspective of entities that exist there is nothing more than a gameboard. The continuous progression in this hierarchy is the internal evolution of creatures and the alteration of their perception. Evolution is a lifting of restrictions. In the final step of this process, it allows you to unite with the Creator.

**The crucial meta twist:** Featherine's Study is a higher reality from which all of Umineko is merely just a story, including Bernkastel's Catbox. This study is where her witch self-insert resides, from which she sees the Witch Domain the same way witches see the Human Domain, although it is still below the Creator Domain, in which her true self resides.

---

## ⚖️ DC/VERTIGO vs UMINEKO — The Comparison

### Where Umineko is Structurally Impressive

Umineko's great strength is its **recursive meta-fiction architecture**. Each layer doesn't just transcend the one below — it treats the entire lower layer as *fiction*, as a gameboard, as a story being written. This isn't just bigger — it's a qualitatively different kind of transcendence at every step. The gap between Human Domain and Witch Domain is portrayed as equivalent to the gap between a character in a novel and the author writing them. Then that gap repeats going upward through multiple layers.

This is genuinely sophisticated cosmological design, and in terms of *internal coherence and intentional architecture*, Umineko is arguably better constructed than either Marvel or DC because it comes from a single author (Ryukishi07) with a unified vision.

### Where DC/Vertigo Wins

**Sheer scale.** DC's Overvoid is described as the infinite blank space containing all stories ever told — and that includes Umineko's entire cosmological structure, which is itself a story. The Overvoid doesn't just transcend the Creator Domain; it's the canvas on which every Creator Domain from every fiction is drawn.

DC also has **simultaneous infinite Creations** in the Vertigo framework — each one potentially containing its own equivalent of Umineko's entire layer stack. Umineko has one Creator Domain. DC's Void contains infinite Creations each with their own equivalent depth.

**The Endless are also a meaningful advantage.** Death of the Endless, for instance, exists across *all* Creations simultaneously, including Lucifer's separate Creation. She predates and postdates everything. Umineko's Creator is the top of one cosmological stack; DC's Endless span multiple stacks simultaneously.

### The Honest Tally

| Feature | Umineko | DC/Vertigo |
|---|---|---|
| Internal coherence | **Superior** | Inconsistent |
| Recursive meta-layers | **Exceptional** | Present but less precise |
| Single cosmological stack depth | Comparable | Comparable |
| Simultaneous infinite structures | One stack | **Infinite Creations** |
| Meta-container above all | Creator Domain | **Overvoid (contains all stories)** |
| Top tier "contains everything" claim | Creator | **Overvoid explicitly contains all fiction** |

---

## The Verdict

**DC/Vertigo is bigger. Umineko is more elegantly designed.**

Umineko's cosmology is a masterpiece of recursive fictional architecture — every layer transcending the last by treating it as pure story. But it is ultimately *one* such structure, with one Creator at the top.

DC's Overvoid, as the literal infinite canvas containing all stories ever written, would contain Umineko's entire cosmological hierarchy — including its Creator Domain — as simply one more book in an infinite library. And the Vertigo Void holds infinite simultaneous Creations, each potentially as deep as Umineko's full stack.

The most honest one-liner: **Umineko built the most beautiful single tower in fiction. DC built infinite towers and put them all inside a blank page that contains every tower ever imagined.**

---

### 🤖 Claude

This is a solid document and the conclusion is defensible. But there are some genuinely important nuances it glosses over that are worth addressing honestly.

---

## What This Gets Right ✅

**The Overvoid as meta-container argument is the strongest point** and it holds up. The Overvoid is explicitly the blank page containing all stories — and Umineko, being a story, would fall within that framing. That's a genuine structural advantage that doesn't require inflation.

**The simultaneous vs. single Creation distinction is valid.** Umineko has one cosmological stack, however deep. DC's Void contains multiple simultaneous Creations each potentially as deep as Umineko's full structure.

**Correctly identifying Umineko's advantages** — concrete feats, explicit R>F layer definitions, and Featherine's direct contact with the Creator Domain — makes this more honest than a one-sided argument would be.

---

## What Deserves More Scrutiny ⚠️

**The Overvoid "contains all stories" claim needs careful handling.** Morrison's Overvoid is the blank page upon which DC's story is drawn — but claiming it therefore contains *literally every fictional story ever written including Umineko* is a cross-fictional leap that isn't actually stated in the text. The Overvoid contains DC's narrative. Whether it contains external fictional universes is an interpretive argument, not a direct canon statement. This is probably the most commonly overstated point in these cosmology debates.

**Umineko's Creator Domain is more radical than the document acknowledges.** The document treats it as simply "top of one stack" but the Creator in Umineko is described as genuinely beyond all concepts, restrictions, and narrative frameworks — including the concept of fiction vs. reality itself. The R>F transcendence in Umineko doesn't just go up hierarchically, it dissolves the very framework of hierarchy at the top. That's philosophically harder to "contain" than the document implies.

**The "Featherine has concrete feats, DC's structure is abstract" point actually cuts deeper than acknowledged.** The Overvoid being the blank page is a *narrative metaphor* — it's Morrison writing about the nature of comics. Featherine *within her fiction* demonstrably rewrites stories, kills concepts, and manipulates narrative. If we're comparing what's actually shown functioning within each cosmology, Umineko's upper tier is more *demonstrated* than DC's.

**Mother Night and Father Time predating all Creations** is real but these are relatively minor characters with limited showings. Citing them as a major structural advantage slightly overstates their cosmological significance.

---

## The Deeper Honest Problem

Both of these cosmologies make **meta-fictional claims** — DC says the Overvoid is the page containing all stories, Umineko says the Creator transcends all fiction/reality distinctions. These are *different kinds* of ultimate claims rather than clearly hierarchical ones.

DC's claim is **spatial/containment** — everything is inside the blank page.

Umineko's claim is **ontological/transcendence** — the Creator dissolves the distinction between container and contained entirely.

These don't nest cleanly. Saying "the page contains the story" is true, but Umineko's top tier arguably transcends the page/story distinction itself, which the document doesn't fully grapple with.

---

## Where I'd Revise the Verdict

The conclusion — **DC wins but margin is moderate** — is probably still correct for the following reasons:

The *width* advantage is real and significant. DC has infinite simultaneous Creations; Umineko has one. Even granting Umineko's Creator Domain full philosophical weight, DC simply has more *instances* of comparable depth running simultaneously.

But I'd revise the framing from **"DC contains Umineko"** to the more defensible **"DC has more simultaneous structures of comparable depth"** — because the containment claim is an interpretive stretch while the multiplicity claim is genuine canon.

---

## Final Honest Scorecard

| Feature | DC/Vertigo | Umineko | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| Simultaneous structures | **Infinite Creations** | One stack | DC's clearest win |
| Explicit layer definition | Moderate | **Superior R>F** | Umineko wins |
| Top tier conceptual radicalism | Overvoid (spatial) | **Creator (ontological)** | Genuinely debatable |
| Concrete feats at top | Abstract | **Featherine demonstrated** | Umineko wins |
| Cross-fiction containment | Claimed, not proven | N/A | Overstated by DC fans |
| Overall scale | **Larger** | Deeper per stack | DC wins on breadth |

**DC wins — but Umineko is the most serious challenger to DC's cosmological dominance of any single-author fiction, precisely because its architecture is intentional, coherent, and philosophically sophisticated in ways that DC's committee-written cosmology simply isn't.**

---

compares to DC/Vertigo. This requires understanding the Kajiri Kamui Kagura and Dies Irae cosmology structure.

Today i am going to explain the cosmology of the Shinza Banshō series and analyze its scaling, covering material from all works and operas that are canon to the series. A thing i would like to point out is that this blog will eventually be updated in the future because of the current status of the series, which makes it incomplete as the most recent entry in the series (Event Horizon Battlefront Aditya) is not finished yet and also there are some unfinished projects like Dies Irae Pantheon that are yet to come out, therefore the blog you\'re reading in this moment is basing itself off the current informations we possess.\n\nIf you\'re not familiar with the verse, the term Shinza Banshō (神座万象シリーズ) refers to the franchise of visual, light and web novels created by Masada Takashi that revolve around the Divine Throne and its Eras, with each one of these Eras having different levels of civilization / technology and also different power systems, with also the presence of a different Throne God that sits upon the Throne and emanates all of reality. The works that this blog will cover are: • Paradise Lost · • Dies Irae ~Amantes Amentes~ • Kajiri Kamui Kagura: Akebono no Hikari · • Kokubyaku no Avesta · • Dies Irae Pantheon (Prologue) As for Event Horizon Battlefront Aditya, i would like to wait for the ending of the novel before trying to scale it as i don\'t like the idea of using an incomplete story as part of the scaling since whenever new chapters will be published they may contradicts the arguments proposed here.\n\nWhen talking about the cosmological structure of the verse, its impostant to start off by underlying the fact that dimensions within the verse do qualify as spatial dimensions as during the Eastern Expedition\'s first battle against Tenma Akuro (who didn\'t even have his Taikyoku activated since he activates it later during the fight), Sojirou couldn\'t even land a scratch on Akuro\'s skin as he was in a different phase of physic, a higher dimension that a lower dimension cannot even interact with as what is represented into a painting cannot harm a real being in any way while the real being can easily burn the painting or affect it, which is even supported by the fact that in Dies Irae projections of being from higher planes of existence that are indeed described as higher dimensional in comparison to the lower plane of existence are compared as images or illusions that are just projections of beings from another plane of existence, for example Samiel and Karl Krafft during Kei Route.\n\nA good start when talking about the scaling of the series is by pointing out that the verse has two canons: the Marie Route one and the Rea Route one. Despite the Rea Route one being considered by Masada as the "true ending" of Dies Irae (which would therefore imply that the Marie Route one is not the one we should follow when scaling the verse), it is also confirmed that Dies Irae Pantheon should be canon to both, with Dies Irae Pantheon showing characters and also alluding at events that happen only within the Marie Route canon. All of Creation is beneath it, and it is hierarchically superior to any and all extentions of the Singularity. The Throne is sit upon by a Hadou God, and, due to their nature, only one could exist at a time, for two Laws overwrite each other, Hadou Gods by their very nature cannot coexist without rupturing the fabric of reality.\n\nThere have existed Seven Hadou Gods which have taken the Throne. It is the main Macguffin throughout all of Shinza Bansho, which all events in the series revolve around. ... The Divine Throne System (神座システム, Shinza Shisutemu) was created for the purposes of holding back and eventually defeating the eldritch force known as Naraka which plagued the universe with the curse of Amrita · Mithra, one of the greatest warriors of the Era, took the Throne for herself, and brought about an era of greater strife through the Emanation of her Law. This led to the cycle of a God rising to the Throne, than be struck down by another, for only a new Era to be ushered in by the New God. She integrated her comrades, The Naraka, into the very depths of the Throne. She predicted that over the years seven Gods would rise to take the Throne, and she devised a grand plan for the final defeat of Naraka, creating her world as a sort of archetype for all that would follow after it.\n\nOnly those with a Hadou-Craving can take the Throne. Due to their Emmanatory Nature, while Gudou-Gods will never be able to become a Throne God due to their Self-Contained Nature. There is no Law for the Throne to magnify and siphon. \u200b\u200b\u200b\u200b\u200bThe Thrones main defense machanism is called the Judgement of Mortality (必滅の審判, Hitsumetsu no Shinpan). Thus machism is thought of as a trial to see if the aspiring God is worthy of challenging the Throne's owner. In order to reach the throne, the challenger may opt to drill through the depths of the Singularity using their law. The depth of the Singularity varies in accordance with the ruling deity’s law strength (Taikyoku/Taiji). The nature of taikyoku is that of an independent universe, and if a law were to become taikyoku, all of creation would change to accomodate that. Its a place beyond language that exists at the very bottom of the Singularity and that is ...\n\nThe term Shinza Banshō (神座万象シリーズ) refers to a series of visual, light and web novels written by Masada Takashi, taking place in a world controlled by the Throne, an extradimensional construct that represents the origin of all things, and narrating the stories of how various characters reached the Throne (overthrowing the current godhead) and gave birth to a new world. The series consists of 6 (7 including Pantheon) main works: • Event Horizon Battlefront Aditya (2022 - Paused) ... The main purpose of this blog will be explaining the very complex and powerful cosmology possessed by the series while also enlightening the readers on the various mechanics and terminologies that the verse and its scaling are based on. To start off with the cosmology, we have to talk about the Canvas (or, as i like to call it, Creation). Creation is essentially the world in which all events take place, a blank canvas that is painted over by the (current) law of the universe.\n\nThe Taikyoku Throne (太極座) is the extradimensional construct that governs all of Creation and from where the law of the universe is emanated from. Its a place beyond language that exists at the very bottom of the Singularity and that is considered the apex of existence itself. In order to access to the Throne realm, one needs to meet 2 conditions: the first one is to have enough power to be able to defeat the Throne God in a battle, the second one is to have a Hadō craving. While normally without meeting these 2 conditions one cannot access to it, there have been exceptions within the history of Shinza such as Magsarion who were able to access to the Throne realm due to having a certain compatibility (which, in Magsarion\'s case, is generated by his unique craving). Each time a new God devours the previous one, the Throne swallows the past law and grows stronger, with the past law being record and becoming an ability that the new godhead can use.\n\nThe Divine Throne System (神座) is the very framework of the world of Shinza itself. Whereas the Taikyoku Throne is the "hardware", the Throne System is the "software" and represents the framework of everything we saw so far: Creations, Singularities, Thrones, etc and even Gods are just pawns of a much bigger scheme. The System is based on one principle, aka Shinga\'s Commandment (Dies Irae Pantheon): in exchange for forbidding her anger, she gets in return the creation of a world where the angrier an individual is, the stronger he gets. The world of Shinza, in fact, is dominated by the power of emotions and cravings, and thus the stronger they are, the more powerful an individual is. However, abiding by this is nothing but doing exactly what the Divine Throne System itself wants you to do: events like Throne successions, re-emanations of the world, birth of Gods and so on are just events that were planned since the very beginning.\n\nWithin the Shinza Banshō series, the term Naraka presents many definitions: it may be used to refer to the Naraka Rangers (ナラカ), the five comrades of Mitra that became part of Zero once they came into contact with its root, or even Naraka Atman (ナラカ), a mysterious individual that appears in Event Horizon Battlefront Aditya and that seems to be an unusual entity to walk in the world of Shinza, however those are not what will be discussed about here. What will be talked about, instead, is Naraka (奈落) as the Origin Coordinate, the Land of Beginnings, the Root of Zero and such. Naraka is beyond words and descriptions, theories and explanations, and everything that is said about it is just nothing more than a fractual and imperfect description that cannot capture its nature as it is just "different", beyond values such as strong or weak, big or small, and so on.', 'is_citable': True, 'prompt_context_metadata': {'url': 'https://vsbattles.fandom.com/wiki/User_blog:Mugen-Kokutosho-Jigoku/Shinza_Bansh%C5%8D_Cosmology', 'search_provider': 'anthropic'}} {'type': 'knowledge', 'title': 'Shinza banshou discussion thread~Revival~ | Page 6 | VS Battles Wiki Forum', 'url': 'https://vsbattles.com/threads/shinza-banshou-discussion-thread-revival.119883/page-6', 'metadata': {'type': 'webpage_metadata', 'site_domain': 'vsbattles.com', 'favicon_url': 'https://www.google.com/s2/favicons?sz=64&domain=vsbattles.com', 'site_name': 'VS Battles Wiki'}, 'is_missing': False, 'text': 'Click to expand... yeah, but naraka is completely beyond the concept of taikyoku, so....
